## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics / nonlinear dynamics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables x (position) and v (velocity) evolving in time t, which is the standard state-space form of (possibly damped/driven) nonlinear harmonic oscillators. Typical physics relationships express dv_dt as a sum of restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and external/parametric forcing (functions of t, x, v).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (Hookean) oscillator (undamped, autonomous): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small oscillations, conservative restoring force)
- Linear viscous damping (Rayleigh dissipation): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-spring-damper near equilibrium)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (high-Re drag or empirical nonlinear damping)
- Coulomb/dry friction (smooth approximation): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * tanh(c2 * v) (sliding friction, stick-slip tendencies)
- Simple pendulum (nonlinear restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) (finite-angle pendulum; x as angle)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Softening with quintic correction: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (higher-order stiffness nonlinearity)
- Driven oscillator (additive periodic forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external harmonic excitation)
- Driven Duffing (nonlinear + forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (chaos/bi-stability regimes)
- Parametrically excited oscillator (Mathieu-type stiffness modulation): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (parametric resonance)
- Van der Pol oscillator (nonlinear self-excited damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (limit-cycle oscillations)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent negative damping + saturation): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (self-oscillation from flow/feedback)
- Li├®nard form (general nonlinear oscillator structure): dv_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * x**2 + c3 * x**4) * v - c4 * x - c5 * x**3 (broad class including Van der Pol/Duffing combinations)
- Potential-gradient (energy-based) model: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (restoring force from polynomial potential plus damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends primarily on x (and not v), often as an odd function in x for symmetric potentials (e.g., -x, -x - x**3).
- Damping signature: terms odd in v (e.g., -v, -v*Abs(v), -tanh(c*v)) dissipate energy and shrink amplitudes over time.
- Self-excitation/limit-cycle signature: damping that changes sign with amplitude (e.g., (1 - c*x**2)*v or v - v**3) creates growth at small amplitude and saturation at large amplitude.
- Nonlinear stiffness signature: higher odd powers of x (x**3, x**5) shift frequency with amplitude and can create multistability (Duffing-type behavior).
- Finite-angle pendulum signature: sin(c*x) restoring force yields amplitude-dependent period and deviates from linearity at larger |x|.
- External driving signature: additive periodic terms in t (cos(c*t), sin(c*t)) inject energy and can lead to resonance/entrainment.
- Parametric resonance signature: coefficients multiplying x that vary periodically in t (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) indicate stiffness modulation and instability tongues.
- Stick-slip/friction signature: non-smooth dependence on v (Abs(v), tanh(c*v)) produces sharp transitions near vŌēł0 and can generate hysteresis-like dynamics.

**GT:** `-1.02670587028003*x**3 - 1.02670587028003*x*exp(-Abs(x)) + 0.947981592038046*sin(t) - 0.712276797350088*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `x**3` 
2. `x*exp(-Abs(x))` ŌĆö depends on x only
3. `sin(t)` ŌĆö depends on t only
4. `sin(v)` ŌĆö depends on v only

Key observations:
- The term `x*exp(-Abs(x))` is a function of x only (not t or v)
- `sin(t)` is a function of t only
- `sin(v)` is a function of v only

Now let me analyze the candidates. Most candidates use exponentials in t (like `exp(c*t)`) and polynomial/absolute value functions of v. The critical question is whether these can reproduce `sin(t)` and `sin(v)` and `x*exp(-Abs(x))`.

**Can `exp(c*t)` terms reproduce `sin(t)`?**
Using Euler's formula: `sin(t) = (exp(it) - exp(-it))/(2i)`. If we allow complex constants, then `c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*exp(c4*t)` with `c2 = i, c4 = -i` could give `sin(t)`. However, in symbolic regression, constants are typically **real**. With real constants, `exp(c*t)` cannot produce `sin(t)` ŌĆö these are fundamentally different basis functions (exponential vs. oscillatory).

Since the problem states constants can be "ANY real number," real exponentials cannot equal `sin(t)`.

**Can polynomial/absolute value functions of v reproduce `sin(v)`?**
`sin(v)` cannot be exactly represented by `v`, `v**3`, `v*Abs(v)`, etc. These are polynomials/piecewise polynomials and are linearly independent from `sin(v)`.

**Can `x*exp(c*t)` reproduce `x*exp(-Abs(x))`?**
No ŌĆö `x*exp(c*t)` depends on both x and t, while `x*exp(-Abs(x))` depends only on x.

**Candidates with `cos(c*t)` or `sin(t)` terms:**
- Candidate 25: has `c8*x*cos(c9*t)` ŌĆö this is `x*cos(t)`, not `sin(t)` alone
- Candidate 27: has `c8*cos(c9*t)` ŌĆö this gives `cos(t)` which equals `sin(t + ŽĆ/2)`, so it can match `sin(t)`. But still can't match `sin(v)` or `x*exp(-Abs(x))`.
- Candidate 42: has `exp(c6*t)*cos(c7*t)` ŌĆö with `c6=0`, this gives `cos(c7*t)` which can match `sin(t)`. But still can't match `sin(v)` or `x*exp(-Abs(x))`.
- Candidate 45, 48: have `v*cos(c*t)` ŌĆö mixed dependence, can't separate.

**None of the candidates** can simultaneously reproduce:
1. `sin(t)` (no candidate has a pure sinusoidal function of t with real exponential constants)
2. `sin(v)` (no candidate has `sin(v)`)
3. `x*exp(-Abs(x))` (no candidate has this x-only term)
